/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:215:Making newly created windows join an existing session
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:218:Normally, after activating a session, if you create new windows/tabs
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:219:they don't belong to the session. If you would prefer to have them belong
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:220:to the currently active session, you can use the :ac:`new_window_with_cwd`
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:221:and :ac:`new_tab_with_cwd` actions instead, like this::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:224:    map kitty_mod+t new_tab_with_cwd
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:227:This will cause newly created windows and tabs to belong to the currently active
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:228:session, if any. Note that adding a window to a session in this way is
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:229:temporary, it does not edit the session file. If you wish to update the
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:230:session file of the currently active session, you can use the following
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:233:    map f5 save_as_session --relocatable --use-foreground-process --match=session:. .
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:236:For even more control of what session a window is added to use
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:237:the :doc:`launch <launch>` command with the :option:`launch --add-to-session`
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:241:Sessions with remote connections
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:244:If you use the :doc:`ssh kitten </kittens/ssh>` to connect to remote computers,
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:245::ac:`save_as_session` is smart enough to save the ssh kitten invocation to your
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:246:session file, preserving the remote working directory and even the currently
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:247:running program on the remote host! Try it, run kitty with::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:249:    kitty -o 'map f1 save_as_session --use-foreground-process --relocatable' --session <(echo "layout vertical\nlaunch\nlaunch")

/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:257:other start some program. Then press :kbd:`F1` to save the session file.

/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:262:Managing multi tab sessions in a single OS Window
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:265:The natural way to organise sessions in kitty is one per :term:`os_window`.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:266:However, if you prefer to manage multiple sessions in a single OS Window, you
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:267:can configure the kitty tab bar to only show tabs that belong to the currently
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:268:active session. To do so, use :opt:`tab_bar_filter` in :file:`kitty.conf` set::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:270:    tab_bar_filter session:~ or session:^$
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:272:This will restrict the tab bar to only showing tabs from the currently active
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:273:session as well tabs that do not belong to any session. Furthermore, when you
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:274:are in a window or tab that does not belong to any session, the tab bar will
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:275:show the tabs from the most recent active session, to maintain context.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:280:Below is the list of all supported keywords in session files along with
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:284:    Change the working directory for all windows in the current tab to
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:286:    containing the session file.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:293:    :ref:`search_syntax` for the syntax for matching expressions.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:301:``focus_tab [tab specifier]``
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:302:    Set which tab should be active (focused) in the current OS Window. The tab
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:304:    match expression. For example, ``focus_tab 0`` will focus the first tab,
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:305:    ``focus_tab 1`` the second tab, and ``focus_tab title:logs`` will focus the
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:306:    tab whose title matches "logs". See :ref:`search_syntax` for the full syntax
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:307:    of match expressions. This is useful for session files that create multiple
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:308:    tabs and want to ensure a specific tab is active when the session is loaded.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:310:``enabled_layouts comma separated list of layout names``
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:311:    Set the layouts allowed in the current tab. Same syntax as
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:312:    :opt:`enabled_layouts`.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:317:    tabs and OS Windows using launch is not supported in session files, use the
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:320:``layout name``
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:321:    Set the layout for the current tab to the specified layout, including any
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:322:    specified options, see :doc:`layouts` for the available layouts and
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:329:``new_tab [tab title]``
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:330:    Create a new tab with the specified title. If no title is specified, the
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:331:    title behaves just as for a regular tab in kitty.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:339:    Set the class part of WM_CLASS or Wayland Application Id for the current OS Window
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/sessions.rst:342:    Set the name part of WM_CLASS or Wayland Window tag for the current OS Window

/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:14:   tab
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:15:     A *tab* refers to a group of :term:`kitty windows <window>`, organized in
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:16:     a :term:`layout`. Every :term:`OS Window <os_window>` contains one or more tabs.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:18:   layout
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:19:     A *layout* is a system of organizing :term:`kitty windows <window>` in
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:20:     groups inside a tab. The layout automatically maintains the size and
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:21:     position of the windows, think of a layout as a tiling window manager for
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:22:     the terminal. See :doc:`layouts` for details.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:27:     :term:`tabs <tab>`. Each tab in turn consists of one or more *kitty
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/glossary.rst:28:     windows* organized in a :term:`layout`.

/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:5:between two connected systems, for example, nested SSH sessions, a serial
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:19:The basic design of this protocol is around transfer "sessions". Since
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:21:filesystem, a session must be approved by the user in the terminal emulator
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:25:There can be either send or receive sessions. In send sessions files are sent
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:26:from remote client to the terminal emulator and vice versa for receive sessions.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:27:Every session basically consists of sending metadata for the files first and
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:28:then sending the actual data. The session is a series of commands, every command
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:29:carrying the session id (which should be a random unique-ish identifier, to
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:30:avoid conflicts). The session is bi-directional with commands going both to and
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:31:from the terminal emulator. Every command in a session also carries an
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:35:Let's look at some simple examples of sessions to get a feel for the protocol.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:47:the client is not allowed to send any more commands for the session.
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:48:The terminal emulator should drop a session if it receives any commands
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:103:the session with::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:107:At this point the terminal commits the session, applying file metadata,
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:191:terminates the session with::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:195:Canceling a session
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:198:A client can decide to cancel a session at any time (for example if the user
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:199:presses :kbd:`ctrl+c`). To cancel a session it sends a ``cancel`` action to the
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:204:The terminal emulator drops the session and sends a cancel acknowledgement::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:219:session command::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:249:    :file:`/C:/some/file.txt`. For maximum portability, the following
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:251:    to try to support them returning errors for non-representable paths)::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:270:    directly executable by the Windows Operating system. There is no attempt to
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:512:When initiating a transfer session the client sends a hash of the password and
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:513:the session id::
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:517:For example, suppose that the session id is ``mysession`` and the
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:519:key above is ``sha256:SHA256("mysession" + ";" + "mypassword")``, which
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:522:    → action=send id=mysession bypass=sha256:192bd215915eeaa8c2b2a4c0f8f851826497d12b30036d8b5b1b4fc4411caf2c
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:530:   exist hash functions harder to compute than SHA256, they are unsuitable as
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:531:   they will introduce a lot of latency to starting a session and in any case
/home/eirikr/Github/tilix/term_analysis/kitty/docs/file-transfer-protocol.rst:555:.. table:: The keys and value types for this protocol
